  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d19c9d2a-e8bf-4070-87c5-e700924bd666'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5762210948693587263">To Libby Mason, Mr. Right has always meant Mr. Rich. A twenty seven-year-old publicist, she's barely able to afford her fashionable and fabulous lifestyle and often has to foot the bill for dates with Struggling Writer Nick, a sexy but perpetually strapped-for-cash guy she's dating (no commitments – really). So when Ed, Britain's wealthiest but stodgiest bachelor, enters t</span>
  <span id="freeText5762210948693587263" style="display:none">To Libby Mason, Mr. Right has always meant Mr. Rich. A twenty seven-year-old publicist, she's barely able to afford her fashionable and fabulous lifestyle and often has to foot the bill for dates with Struggling Writer Nick, a sexy but perpetually strapped-for-cash guy she's dating (no commitments – really). So when Ed, Britain's wealthiest but stodgiest bachelor, enters the picture, her idea of the fairy tale romance is turned on it's head. <br /><br /><b>Mr. Maybe</b> is the tale of her heartfelt but hilarious deliberation, irresistibly chronicled by bestselling author <b>Jane Green</b>. On one hand, Nick makes up for his low bank-account balance by his performance in the sack, or in the bathtub, as the case may be. But life with him means little more than nightly trips to the bar, a dark and grungy apartment, and plenty of dull political tirades to boot. But those blue eyes, and that tender heart...<br /><br />On the other hand, there's Ed, whose luxurious house and gargantuan bank account are quite tempting to the starving Libby. But his unsavory mustache and bumbling ways make Libby wonder if the platinum AMEX and unlimited "retail therapy" are worth it. He may have fallen in love with her at first sight, but nothing seems to solve his lackluster performance in the sack – even speed reading The Joy of Sex. When the diamond shopping commences, Libby is forced to realize that the time for "maybe" is up. <br /><br /><i>Taking romantic comedy to a hip, sparkling new level, <b>Mr. Maybe</b> is a classic tale of what happens to one girl when her heart and her head aren't looking for the same thing. With a laugh and minute and a heroine whose struggles in the dating jungle will remind you of your own, Mr. Maybe is a story that all will leave you smitten.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5762210948693587263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lilly" href="/user/show/24423-lilly">Lilly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203580152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4487179647269732544">The best thing about this book was that it makes you realize that anyone really CAN get published! They should really file it under "inspiration".<br/><br/>I know, I know, I got what I deserved. I just wanted a fun summer read and I loved her book Jemima J, but this was *complete* garbage. The characters were shallow and unlikeable (at one point the main character realizes she is literally prostituting herself out). She is such a self-satisfied whiner that I found myself actively rooting *against* her. <br/><br/>An</span>
  <span id="freeText4487179647269732544" style="display:none">The best thing about this book was that it makes you realize that anyone really CAN get published! They should really file it under "inspiration".<br /><br />I know, I know, I got what I deserved. I just wanted a fun summer read and I loved her book Jemima J, but this was *complete* garbage. The characters were shallow and unlikeable (at one point the main character realizes she is literally prostituting herself out). She is such a self-satisfied whiner that I found myself actively rooting *against* her. <br /><br />And just when you can't hate them more, an awkward, explicit, and completely unnecessary sex scene is thrown in for good measure.<br /><br />I wish this had been a Choose Your Own Adventure where I could show up in the final scene and shoo the guy away (I won't spoil it and tell you who the guy is, because if after this you still read it, you deserve to suffer). <br /><br />I want to throw this book away but maybe I'll save it as a birthday gift for someone I really hate.<br /><br />Blech.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4487179647269732544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2007161208" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2007161208" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2007161208?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6320367-mr-maybe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=2017-library-love-challenge">2017-library-love-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=tbr-2017">tbr-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2007161208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3020269377528609071">This was one Jane Green book from her chick lit days I never read. I wondered why I never bought this and now I know why. I must have read the sample and said no thank you. That was a smart decision. I am kind of horrified at how bad this book was. The main character was awful, so were two of her love interests. Her friend was having issues (serious ones) that she ignored. Her mother made Mrs. Bennett in Pride and Prejudice look like a saint. I mean my God. That's a terrible bar to be lower than</span>
  <span id="freeText3020269377528609071" style="display:none">This was one Jane Green book from her chick lit days I never read. I wondered why I never bought this and now I know why. I must have read the sample and said no thank you. That was a smart decision. I am kind of horrified at how bad this book was. The main character was awful, so were two of her love interests. Her friend was having issues (serious ones) that she ignored. Her mother made Mrs. Bennett in Pride and Prejudice look like a saint. I mean my God. That's a terrible bar to be lower than. So why did I keep reading? I kept wondering how bad could it get. It got really bad.<br /><br />Told in the first person, we have Libby Mason who is looking for love in all the wrong places. Libby is told constantly by her terrible mother that she's not worth a damn until she gets married and married to a man with money. And though Libby has dated (and frankly based on the way she acts, I can see why men left her butt) she is still looking to date a rich man who can keep her in designer clothes and a million dollar mansion. Working in publicity has Libby next to the wealthy, but she's not wealthy. <br /><br />When she goes out with friends, she runs into Nick (who she has met before). She and Nick have insta-chemistry/lust in this one and though Libby knows it won't work out, thinks she is capable of just having a fling with Nick (she's not). <br /><br />Nick is everything that Libby doesn't want, he's jobless, poor, and doesn't see a problem with dressing like he's homeless. But you know, hot sex, yadda yadda yadda. When Libby starts to catch feelings for Nick, he realizes they should stop while they are ahead. Libby then ends up meeting her rich man and wonders if he is the one for her.<br /><br />I just can't with this book. Nick is a jerk and so are his friends. Libby is a jerk too though so I don't know who wins that contest. I have never read a book about so many unlikable people in my life. And the only one I felt sorry for was the guy Libby ends up dating after Nick, Ed. Ed wines and dines Libby and she's angry that he's bad in bed, has a gross mustache, etc. but is still happy to get all the flowers and presents the guy showers onto her. Her mother practically offers herself up to him if he will keep dating Libby.<br /><br />I think in the end I should be happy about follow your heart or something, but wow they all suck. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3020269377528609071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_173023156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173023156" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5212582-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540105335p2/5212582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173023156?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/5212582-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5212582-lee?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173023156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15223090345361415647">If you want poignancy, you won't get that in this book. This is your average chick literature, with a protagonist whose only goal in mind is to end up with the guy of her dreams.<br/><br/>Now, you may be thinking, why the fuck do I like this book? For starters, I have already breached below my expectations for a book when it comes to chick literature. I already expect a common plot, a protagonist with an I'm-ugly-as-fuck self-esteem and some twisted, completely shallow "hindrance" why the protagonist won'</span>
  <span id="freeText15223090345361415647" style="display:none">If you want poignancy, you won't get that in this book. This is your average chick literature, with a protagonist whose only goal in mind is to end up with the guy of her dreams.<br /><br />Now, you may be thinking, why the fuck do I like this book? For starters, I have already breached below my expectations for a book when it comes to chick literature. I already expect a common plot, a protagonist with an I'm-ugly-as-fuck self-esteem and some twisted, completely shallow "hindrance" why the protagonist won't be with the man of his dreams. So when I read this, I didn't expect depth at all.<br /><br />I cried twice in this book mainly because it borders on something most of us have experienced so many times in life. PAIN. I cried with Libby when Nick left her, albeit he genuinely likes her. This is something that I experienced in my life, someone leaving me even though he still loved me and all that jazz. I cried with Libby when Cat accompanied Nick to a party thrown by Sal and Paul. Now, seeing the love of your life with another woman also takes the edge on the pain scale.<br /><br />I guess I'm a huge romantic who's hardwired for drama. That's why I gave it four stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15223090345361415647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_491561515" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491561515" />
    <a title="Monica Shoshanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15971795-monica-shoshanna"><img alt="Monica Shoshanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603628649p2/15971795.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/491561515?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monica Shoshanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monica Shoshanna" href="/user/show/15971795-monica-shoshanna">Monica Shoshanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer491561515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8990692435226933236">This book was utter garbage, how do books like this get published. Firstly I didn't really warm to any of the characters and I couldn't stand the main character Libby; I found her really shallow, unpleasant and materialistic. She really proves how feminism hasn't changed anything if woman are still intent on marrying rich men. I didn't care for any of the characters, especially Nick, the guy who Libby is in love with. I didn't warm to him at all, he's just your classic commitment phobe who can't</span>
  <span id="freeText8990692435226933236" style="display:none">This book was utter garbage, how do books like this get published. Firstly I didn't really warm to any of the characters and I couldn't stand the main character Libby; I found her really shallow, unpleasant and materialistic. She really proves how feminism hasn't changed anything if woman are still intent on marrying rich men. I didn't care for any of the characters, especially Nick, the guy who Libby is in love with. I didn't warm to him at all, he's just your classic commitment phobe who can't make his mind up. I really didn't like him. The only character I felt slightly sorry for was Ed, the rich guy who Libby pursues and uses his for money, whilst he genuinely adores her. Secondly I found the story too long and at times dragged out a bit too much. I found the book rather yawnsome and it wasnt that intriguing. I only read it quickly because I dont finish books very often and I wanted to get it over and done with. I skimmed a bit at times because I just found it dull. It's not very well written at all; its easy to read but I found the style sloppy. So my conclusion is that this book is forgettable trash which I wouldn't recommend to anyone.<br /><br />Grade: E</span>
  <a data-text-id="8990692435226933236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20608754" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20608754" />
    <a title="Yulia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/185835-yulia"><img alt="Yulia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508793572p2/185835.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20608754?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yulia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yulia" href="/user/show/185835-yulia">Yulia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/185835-yulia?shelf=here-chicky-chicky">here-chicky-chicky</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer20608754&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20608754" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18047752849641200508">Here's the usual dilemma in chick-lit novels: A woman struggles to choose between a wealthy man she has no connection with and a poor man she loves. She chooses the poor man and he ends up already being or quickly becoming wealthy. We're all happy. The end. But what if the woman chooses the poor man and, goodness gracious, he remains poor (but lovable). What happens then? I know, but I'm not telling. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82863995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82863995" />
    <a title="Shy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3094614-shy"><img alt="Shy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419064291p2/3094614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82863995?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shy" href="/user/show/3094614-shy">Shy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140276510" href="/book/show/31109.Mr_Maybe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=on-kindle">on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=genre_romance">genre_romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=black-list">black-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82863995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7239934610158459168">I don’t know what to expect when I first picked up this novel. Jane Green was not one of the authors that I’m familiar with so I thought it is good to try something new. Sadly to say though, the result was rather frustrating.<br/><br/>The book started off OK but once I passed the first hundred-page, I literally start to yawn. The predictability of the plots and some annoying characters really turned off my interest but still, I continued reading in hope that there might be something that could spark my in</span>
  <span id="freeText7239934610158459168" style="display:none">I don’t know what to expect when I first picked up this novel. Jane Green was not one of the authors that I’m familiar with so I thought it is good to try something new. Sadly to say though, the result was rather frustrating.<br /><br />The book started off OK but once I passed the first hundred-page, I literally start to yawn. The predictability of the plots and some annoying characters really turned off my interest but still, I continued reading in hope that there might be something that could spark my interest back on. Nevertheless, nothing really happen other than me getting more and more annoyed with the main character, Libby. Her hopeless, indecisive manner truly crawled under my skin and the way she measured a guy by the stack of money in his pocket was downright sickening. Even though she was just a fictional character, I do not think that it is wise to make a woman looks this daft.<br /><br />So, needless to say, I am very disappointed with this book and will definitely not going to recommend this book to anyone.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7239934610158459168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_148820233" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148820233" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1855488-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233935384p2/1855488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148820233?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/1855488-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1855488-rachel?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148820233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3843743222975237329">Over the years I’ve come to accept the fact that sometimes I’m in the mood to read unapologetic fluff. For me, that usually means a British rom/com filled with women who wear Jigsaw suits to their jobs as television presenters, who eat takeaway curries in their garden flats and take mini cab’s to meet their girlfriends at smart pubs at the weekend. I’ve always enjoyed these books with their pleasant and predictable plots where funny, slightly shallow, girls make messes of their love-lives, fight</span>
  <span id="freeText3843743222975237329" style="display:none">Over the years I’ve come to accept the fact that sometimes I’m in the mood to read unapologetic fluff. For me, that usually means a British rom/com filled with women who wear Jigsaw suits to their jobs as television presenters, who eat takeaway curries in their garden flats and take mini cab’s to meet their girlfriends at smart pubs at the weekend. I’ve always enjoyed these books with their pleasant and predictable plots where funny, slightly shallow, girls make messes of their love-lives, fight with their trilling mums, count on their friends, and end up with a grumpy by ardent Mr. Right. They kiss and my girlie brain flashes back to Darcy and Elizabeth (and Darcy and Bridget for that matter…) and the book ends on happily ever after. <br /><br />Jane Green’s Mr. Maybe is precisely that sort of book, only I hated it. There was one major missing element: A likeable protagonist. The “heroine” is Libby, a young woman so shallow and so money grubbing that she is ready to walk down the aisle with a man who she finds not only physically repulsive but irritating and unlikeable. He is, of course, in Libby’s parlance “massively wealthy.” Libby’s better advisors- her best friend, her brother, and her father- tell Libby gently, and then not so gently, that this man is NOT for her. Only her heartless, dim mother thinks that Libby is making a wise decision. Of course, Green provides some explanation of Libby’s delusion- her heart was recently broken, she’s never had someone “treat her well….” But still. She feels nauseas when this man kisses her, and smothered by his attention. Of course, there is another man in the picture: Funny, sexy, kind, but, of course, tragically poor Nick. I don’t think I need to connect the dots for you plot-wise- it’s not exactly a nail biter. <br /><br />This book left me irritated at its pathetic protagonist and at the writer who created her. Looking back though, I wonder is this book was really any worse than Green’s other books that I read and liked about 9 years ago? Is Libby was really any shallower than say Becky Bloomwood, or even Miss Jones herself? It may be that now that I’m in my early 30’s (ugh) rather than my early 20’s, these fairy tale romances between naïve women and stolid men don’t work for my anymore. I may have…finally… outgrown them. It seems impossible, but here we are. So it looks like I’m in the market for a new kind of fluff. Maybe cat themed mysteries? Or novels about quilting societies? Or what’s that one about quirky, church-going townspeople? Hmmm…. Let me know. I’m open to suggestions.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3843743222975237329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_50585203" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50585203" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2166210-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434400110p2/2166210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer50585203&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer50585203" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13697536094589093501">Check out the cover, wouldn't he at least be Mr. Right Now?<br/><br/>So Libby is 27 and single and wanting to have a better half. After meeting Nick as more than an acquaintance the two get a hot fling going on. He came to her flat on the first night and took a bath and they did it right there in her tub. I almost needed a cold shower after this chapter! Needless to say I was hooked from the beginning.<br/>Libby you rock. I love how Jane Green writes the characters thoughts and then what the character says and</span>
  <span id="freeText13697536094589093501" style="display:none">Check out the cover, wouldn't he at least be Mr. Right Now?<br /><br />So Libby is 27 and single and wanting to have a better half. After meeting Nick as more than an acquaintance the two get a hot fling going on. He came to her flat on the first night and took a bath and they did it right there in her tub. I almost needed a cold shower after this chapter! Needless to say I was hooked from the beginning.<br />Libby you rock. I love how Jane Green writes the characters thoughts and then what the character says and how Libby does often speak her mind. Girl after my own heart.<br /><br />Alas the gorgeous Nick, who is an amazing kisser and even hotter in bed, or wherever they are when they do it, tells her from the start he is not ready for a relationship. And so it goes and before they know it they are in a non relationship relationship so Nick has to end it because he is not ready for what is already in their face.<br /><br />Of course Libby is devastated. He is gorgeous, a great lover, and becoming a great friend, and gets along great with her friends. This was supposed to be a fun fling but when everything feels so right why can't it be the right time for a relationship?<br />Then her bff takes her out because the best way to get over someone naturally is to get under someone else. A man by the name of Ed gives Libby his card and asks to take her to dinner sometime. He phones, she's not quite sure but of course she accepts when she learns hes beyond rich and one of London's most eligible bachelors.<br /><br />Its predictable, of course shes always wanted to be the rich man's wife and here he is, but can she ever get gorgeous broke Nick off her mind? Um not after that bath, neither can I hehehe. So its not about the men but our dearest Libby and how she goes through all the emotions all of us single girls go through. A great fun read which I know is always described as a "beach read" but in the beginnings of spring why can't everyone just accept us girls love these easy to read stories any time of year? Sorry to say goodbye to Libby but there's so much of me in her and all us single ladies it really isn't a true goodbye.<br /><br />Very fun read!!! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13697536094589093501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2073711592445332994" style="display:none">I have wanted to read this book for like ever and I was so happy that I finally got it! However, I just wish that I ended up liking it a lot more. Now don't get me wrong - I liked it but the MC just rubbed me the wrong way for most of the book. I just wish she wasn't who she was the entire book and then maybe I would've liked her - but.. uh.. yeah.. I totally didn't. <br /><br />Then there's Nick, who is the love of Libby's black heart. Honestly, if the book didn't have Libby or Nick and had some more likable and relatable characters then <i>Mr. Maybe</i> would've gotten a lot more stars and a way better review.<br /><br />I feel like I need a happy book or happy juice to make my day shine a little bit brighter. <br /></span>

    <a title="Ellen Horn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3471888-ellen-horn"><img alt="Ellen Horn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546285162p2/3471888.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157105331?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157105331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6997894250034593969">I read this book during my obsession with British authors period, along with coming off of a break up. And let me tell you, it didn't disappoint! This book is wildly funny and really tells the story of dating during your twenties. Libby, who has no idea what is important in a relationship, is a loveable heroine. She becomes strong and you can feel yourself falling in love with her. The journey she takes is one that allows the reader to re-examine their own dating history. Pointing out that every</span>
  <span id="freeText6997894250034593969" style="display:none">I read this book during my obsession with British authors period, along with coming off of a break up. And let me tell you, it didn't disappoint! This book is wildly funny and really tells the story of dating during your twenties. Libby, who has no idea what is important in a relationship, is a loveable heroine. She becomes strong and you can feel yourself falling in love with her. The journey she takes is one that allows the reader to re-examine their own dating history. Pointing out that everyone has Nick and there's always an Ed around the corner. Her crazy stories and escapades are not only hilarious but begin to become part of your own life. Suddenly, you become Libby and your best friend becomes Jules. You are able to identify with both love interests and your heart breaks every time Libby's does.<br /><br />This book is recommended for anyone who needs to remember the importance of growing up and what matters in a relationship. Libby is a sort of every woman and really becomes identifiable. She weaves a tapestry of hilarity and love. Sit down with a big cup of tea, your favorite snack and enjoy!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6997894250034593969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1320376666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13129177416147813761"><i>"I’ve come home. It’s difficult to explain, but there is something so familiar, so comfortable, so right about this moment, it suddenly feels like I am exactly where I should be, at exactly the right time, with exactly the right person."</i><br/><br/><br/>I first read Mr. Maybe during my major Brit Lit-love fest of the early-2000s. More than a decade later...and I'm happy to say that I still love this book. <br/><br/>Mr. Maybe is more women's fic (or chick lit, as we used to call it then) than romance. While yes, Libby does</span>
  <span id="freeText13129177416147813761" style="display:none"><i>"I’ve come home. It’s difficult to explain, but there is something so familiar, so comfortable, so right about this moment, it suddenly feels like I am exactly where I should be, at exactly the right time, with exactly the right person."</i><br /><br /><br />I first read Mr. Maybe during my major Brit Lit-love fest of the early-2000s. More than a decade later...and I'm happy to say that I still love this book. <br /><br />Mr. Maybe is more women's fic (or chick lit, as we used to call it then) than romance. While yes, Libby does experience passion and infatuation and ultimately love, this is the story of a young woman finding her own self-worth and learning what she and her heart deserves. <br /><br />Mr. Maybe is early, yet classic, Jane Green. The protagonist is an unapologetically real and honest woman who comes to life-changing realizations about herself, there is an excellent cast of secondary characters; there is a man who is not from a fairy tale, but is winning in his own way; and there is laughter. Mr. Maybe was just as wonderful as I remembered. I had a wonderful time reading it again all these years later. And wow, what more could I ask for? <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13129177416147813761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Hemavathy DM Suppiah-Devi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35775126-hemavathy-dm-suppiah-devi"><img alt="Hemavathy DM Suppiah-Devi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591944847p2/35775126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1591309660?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hemavathy DM Suppiah-Devi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hemavathy DM Suppiah-Devi" href="/user/show/35775126-hemavathy-dm-suppiah-devi">Hemavathy DM Suppiah-Devi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1591309660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer151880302297792888">This is not one of JG's best, but it sort of grows on you over time. And this really is a clever little book and insightfully too. How often have got into something that wasn't right for us because we wanted it so terribly to be right?<br/><br/>I could understand Libby's dilemma. Which woman doesn't want a guy who's good in bed and has the financial backing to help? And Libby isn't a bimbo. She has a job of her own that she works really hard at, and also happens to adore fashion. <br/><br/>I really didn't like Nick</span>
  <span id="freeText151880302297792888" style="display:none">This is not one of JG's best, but it sort of grows on you over time. And this really is a clever little book and insightfully too. How often have got into something that wasn't right for us because we wanted it so terribly to be right?<br /><br />I could understand Libby's dilemma. Which woman doesn't want a guy who's good in bed and has the financial backing to help? And Libby isn't a bimbo. She has a job of her own that she works really hard at, and also happens to adore fashion. <br /><br />I really didn't like Nick in the first part of the book. He wasn't her equal in many ways, as she spent most of her time paying for the dates and mothering him. Also, it was pretty obvious that he wanted the fun but wasn't ready for commitment. <br /><br />Ed was there to salve her ego. But even though he was quite a snob, and had zero personality, and was really boring. But I could understand her going out with him as I've dated guys like Ed. it's the curiosity factor. <br /><br />Libby is unapologetically honest about being shallow. She likes nice things and she wants to be treated nice. She's also honest about her insecurities, and trying to adapt to each new boyfriend like a chameleon to get him to love her. <br /><br />It's really about loving herself, as cliched as it is. <br /><br />And honestly, her mum is horrible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="151880302297792888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Realized a chapter or two in that I'd read it before. <br /><br />Woman wants to meet Mr. Right. Meets Mr. Hot who makes clear he does not want long term relationship. She thinks she won't get emotionally involved, but she does. He breaks up with her. She immediately meets Mr. Moneybags - one of London's most eligible bachelor's. Her mother starts planning the wedding. He proposes surprisingly soon. She feels it's not quite right. Realize Mr. Hot is the right guy. He realizes he made a mistake. She dumps Mr. Moneybags and resumes relationship with Mr. Hot. <br /><br />Easy summer read. Not horrible, but too predictable. Mr. Moneybags is drawn as such an awful mismatch for her that one knows from the start it will not last. </span>

I just wish the book had focused more on the interesting relationship than the boring one. The interesting relationship was secondary in this book, and it was frustrating to have to wait for it to re-appear all the time.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_692699200" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/692699200" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/692699200?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shamsh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shamsh" href="/user/show/1879958-shamsh">Shamsh</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1709567285040587295" style="display:none">Hm. Can I use MC words to describe how I feel? "I love it. But I don't fancy it."<br />I have mixed feelings about this book. I've enjoyed reading it and some parts were even funny. But the main issue I had was the main character - Libby. There were so many times, then I wanted to shake her to wake the hell up or just to slap her to make sence. The way she acted or even thought about dating/relationships was just so so... ugh... I don't even know what word I am looking for. But maybe that was the point? To show how some girls/woman changes and does stupid things to fit in and "make work" hopeless relationships for the wrong reasons. I don't know. I'll have to sit on this one for a bit, but for now I more or lest think 2.5 or 3 stars.</span>

<div id="review_956722319" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956722319" />
    <a title="Allie Burke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31381292-allie-burke"><img alt="Allie Burke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429022599p2/31381292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/956722319?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allie Burke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allie Burke" href="/user/show/31381292-allie-burke">Allie Burke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer956722319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4387653643280749460">Jane Green is one of those authors who writes a bunch of solid romances that are okay and sort of end up blending into one another instead of writing one or two really, really good books (I just rated <i>Bookends</i> three stars because I honestly couldn't remember what it was about), but <i>Mr. Maybe</i> did stick out to me a bit if only for its mild moments of hilarity and Mr. Oh So Sexy (Nick, aka Mr. Maybe) with no job, but being Mr. Oh So Sexy nonetheless. Libby annoyed me, because for some reason Mr. Ri</span>
  <span id="freeText4387653643280749460" style="display:none">Jane Green is one of those authors who writes a bunch of solid romances that are okay and sort of end up blending into one another instead of writing one or two really, really good books (I just rated <i>Bookends</i> three stars because I honestly couldn't remember what it was about), but <i>Mr. Maybe</i> did stick out to me a bit if only for its mild moments of hilarity and Mr. Oh So Sexy (Nick, aka Mr. Maybe) with no job, but being Mr. Oh So Sexy nonetheless. Libby annoyed me, because for some reason Mr. Right means Mr. Rich (who does that, really?) and she's all excited about marrying some guy she barely knows - not to mention who Totally Sucks at the Art of Pleasuring a Woman - because he gave her some rock she's dragging around on her finger, but whatever, people are weird, and I'm convinced I'll never figure them out.<br /><br />I did enjoy this book because Green is not afraid to make fun of Americans (why not, everyone else does) and My Favorite Thing is when I learn something from a fiction novel i.e. what 'The Dole' means, which prepared me for the day my ex-boyfriend asked me halfway into Some English Movie "WTF is a DOLE", to which I responded "unemployment", to which our mutual BFF responded "I don't even want to know how the fuck you know that", to which my ex responded "she probably read it in a book". <br /><br />Yeah. <br /><br />Anyway, <i>Mr. Maybe</i> is somewhat funny and somewhat relatable even if you're an American and not an English Person Making Fun of Americans, and has Mr. Oh So Sexy in it, so worth a read for those who are aware that Jane Green is not out to win some award for The Utmost Literary Work of Art or whatever (that I know of). Again, see: <i>Bookends</i>. Damn, I really want to know what that book is about now. That's going to bug me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4387653643280749460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_165082714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165082714" />
    <a title="Claire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5362894-claire"><img alt="Claire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434918031p2/5362894.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165082714?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire" href="/user/show/5362894-claire">Claire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/13602039-mr-maybe">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165082714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7163695981148349799">*River Song voice* Spoilers!<br/><br/>I hate chick-lit. I really do. It’s empty and boring and cliche and annoying. But yet here I am, reading yet another romance novel. I thought this one would be different. I hoped this one would be different. It wasn’t.<br/><br/>The main character is Libby, who (like most main characters of chick-lit novels) has had trouble with men. Then she meets cute guy Nick, who is so, so, good in bed and really funny and smart, but she hates his lifestyle and his friends and his profession</span>
  <span id="freeText7163695981148349799" style="display:none">*River Song voice* Spoilers!<br /><br />I hate chick-lit. I really do. It’s empty and boring and cliche and annoying. But yet here I am, reading yet another romance novel. I thought this one would be different. I hoped this one would be different. It wasn’t.<br /><br />The main character is Libby, who (like most main characters of chick-lit novels) has had trouble with men. Then she meets cute guy Nick, who is so, so, good in bed and really funny and smart, but she hates his lifestyle and his friends and his profession. So they break up and she cries about it for like four chapters. Then she meets rich and eligible Ed, who she cannot stand being around, but he has the one thing she wants most: money. So of course she has a choice to make, the poor guy who she really loves or the rich guy who will buy her whatever she wants. And spoiler alert! She gets with the guy she loves AND he conveniently gets rich at the end. WHO CARES.<br /><br />The main character was incredibly annoying. Libby would make a decision, complain about said decision for the entirety of her experience, and then realize, OH! That was a great decision! It gets old. Like be smarter, please.<br /><br />And the ending was completely cliche (which I should have expected) but for once I want a character in a chick-lit novel to make the wrong decision. I wanted her to choose the money over the guy she loves and be unfulfilled. I wanted her to regret her decision and weep in agony when Nick gets rich and she’s stuck in a loveless marriage. For once I want human error to be present in a romance novel, I don’t want happily ever after, I want flaws.<br /><br />2/5 stars<br /><br />Book review blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://thebookgirlblog.wordpress.com/">http://thebookgirlblog.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7163695981148349799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_93118269" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93118269" />
    <a title="Jaimie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3407177-jaimie"><img alt="Jaimie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422470721p2/3407177.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93118269?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaimie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaimie" href="/user/show/3407177-jaimie">Jaimie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3407177-jaimie?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93118269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14866823826030921404">Libby Mason is a lovable character who will have you laughing out loud at her internal monologue. She has all the ingredients for a great female lead: stylish wardrobe, sassy attitude, great best friend, and an overbearing mother. Jane Green makes me want to move to London, yesterday. Nick is a hottie with a body and spells t-r-o-u-b-l-e for poor Libby right from the get go. While she has convinced herself that she just wants a fling the reader knows better as does her bff Jules. While the blurb</span>
  <span id="freeText14866823826030921404" style="display:none">Libby Mason is a lovable character who will have you laughing out loud at her internal monologue. She has all the ingredients for a great female lead: stylish wardrobe, sassy attitude, great best friend, and an overbearing mother. Jane Green makes me want to move to London, yesterday. Nick is a hottie with a body and spells t-r-o-u-b-l-e for poor Libby right from the get go. While she has convinced herself that she just wants a fling the reader knows better as does her bff Jules. While the blurb makes Libby out to be fairly shallow and materialistic as a reader I didn't get that. Sure she fantasizes about being rich and the lifestyle that would grant her but who doesn't? The rollercoaster of a relationship between Libby and Nick feels real as much as her relationship with Ed feels false. There are parts of her story that I think every woman could relate to when thinking about her own dating history. The sex is pretty hot - a little hotter than Green's usual fair or maybe that is just because Nick is so yummy. The smut-o-meter on this one is probably high enough that I would say no under 16 readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14866823826030921404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('huS+2pE1deqvwLa8TRgWMODsshKoRq8UFTVVe9b2W0z7IYuIZhXnDR+zzwn4e/yTVU3NQRjtSpaXUN94gyufEg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Geqm7LTu+NjCkw8uV6Q8w8xwb+/gogpfItwqHKMiZAZkL5O+Q85qP3Lgdpvix9ZgedEQvFAJ792guaAf9v+gWA==')})
  }

Andrea Sachs, a small-town girl fresh out of college, lands the job “a million girls would die for.” Hired as the assistant to Miranda Priestly, the high-profile, fabulously successful editor of &quot;Runway &quot;magazine, Andrea finds herself in an office that shouts &quot;Prada! Armani! Versace!&quot; at every turn, a world populated by impossibly thin, heart-wrenchingly stylish women and beautiful men clad in fine-ribbed turtlenecks and tight leather pants that show off their lifelong dedication to the gym. With breathtaking ease, Miranda can turn each and every one of these hip sophisticates into a scared, whimpering child. THE DEVIL WEARS PRADA gives a rich and hilarious new meaning to complaints about “The Boss from Hell.” Narrated in Andrea’s smart, refreshingly disarming voice, it traces a deep, dark, devilish view of life at the top only hinted at in gossip columns and over Cosmopolitans at the trendiest cocktail parties. From sending the latest, not-yet-in-stores Harry Potter to Miranda’s children in Paris by private jet, to locating an unnamed antique store where Miranda had at some point admired a vintage dresser, to serving lattes to Miranda at precisely the piping hot temperature she prefers, Andrea is sorely tested each and every day—and often late into the night with orders barked over the phone. She puts up with it all by keeping her eyes on the prize: a recommendation from Miranda that will get Andrea a top job at any magazine of her choosing. As things escalate from the merely unacceptable to the downright outrageous, however, Andrea begins to realize that the job a million girls would die for may just kill her. <span id="freeTextContainer4546894618210254185">Jane Green's eighteenth novel, Falling, is soon to be released with Berkley/Penguin; she is the author of sixteen previous New York Times Bestselling novels, and known as one of the world's leading authors in women's fiction, with over ten million books in print, and translations in over 25 languages. <br/><br/>Previous novels have included The Beach House, Second Chance, Jemima J, and Tempting Fate.<br/><br/>She joi</span>
  <span id="freeText4546894618210254185" style="display:none">Jane Green's eighteenth novel, Falling, is soon to be released with Berkley/Penguin; she is the author of sixteen previous New York Times Bestselling novels, and known as one of the world's leading authors in women's fiction, with over ten million books in print, and translations in over 25 languages. <br /><br />Previous novels have included The Beach House, Second Chance, Jemima J, and Tempting Fate.<br /><br />She joined the ABC News team to write their first enhanced digital book— about the history of Royal marriages, then joined ABC News as a live correspondent covering Prince William’s wedding to Kate Middleton. <br /><br /> A former journalist in the UK, she has had her own radio show on BBC Radio London, and is a regular contributor on radio and TV, including as well as regularly appearing on television shows including Good Morning America, The Martha Stewart show, and The Today Show.<br /><br />Together with writing books and blogs, she contributes to various publications, both online and print, including anthologies and novellas, and features for The Huffington Post, The Sunday Times, Cosmopolitan and Self. She has taught at writers conferences, and does regular keynote speaking, and has a weekly column in The Lady magazine, England’s longest running weekly magazine.<br /><br />A graduate of the French Culinary Institute in New York, Green is bringing out her first cookbook: Good Taste , with Berkley in October 2016. <br /><br />She is a storyteller for The Moth radio hour on NPR, <br />and lives in Westport, Connecticut with her husband and their blended family. When she is not writing, cooking, gardening, filling her house with friends and herding chickens, she is usually thanking the Lord for caffeine-filled energy drinks. <br /><br />A cancer survivor, she continues to raise awareness for Malignant Melanoma, Hashimoto's Disease, and Lyme Disease.<br /><br /><br />Jane's Facebook page:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Jane-Green/28942670587">http://www.facebook.com/pages/Jane-Gr...</a><br /><br /><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i> </span>

I think it's become too handy, a useful phrase that men can bandy about whenever they feel like being assholes. And sure, I do believe there are some men who are genuinely terrified of commitment, but there aren't that many, and for the most part I think it's that they haven't met the right woman yet. Because if a man, no matter how scared he professed to be, met the woman of his dreams, he wouldn't want to let her go, would he? And sure, he might not want to actually get married, but if he were madly in love and risked losing her, he'd do it, wouldn't he?<br /><br />That's what I think, anyway.&rdquo;</span>
